Muling Coal Mine's Business Situation Last Year 70

Net Profit Increased to 2.4 Million Yuan. Jilin Dispatch: The Sino-Russian joint venture Muling Coal Mine Company held its twelfth board meeting in Harbin on May 12 to report on the business situation for 1918 and discuss how to allocate profits. The Provincial Government sent Ma Deen, Director of the Agricultural and Mining Bureau, to attend. According to the report, the company sold a total of 311,165.048 tons of coal this year, earning a profit of 1,956,009.47 yuan. The Muling Railway earned a net profit of 435,412.78 yuan, for a total profit of 2,391,422.25 yuan. After deducting 15% of the coal sales as a public reserve fund and 20% of the railway's net profit for education and industry,

bonuses should be appropriately awarded to those who contributed to the work in accordance with the regulations. Although the extraction of bonuses is stipulated in the board's meeting rules, the amount varies. In 1917, 1.15% was extracted as bonuses for staff. Last year, the border defense was strained, and the mine was at the forefront of the conflict. All staff members worked diligently and selflessly day and night, making extraordinary contributions. It was agreed that 14% should be extracted as bonuses, as in previous years, with 12% distributed as follows: 4.61% to senior staff and 7.39% to all junior and middle-level staff. The Jilin Provincial Government should receive a total of 1,004,710 yuan from coal sales, railway net profit, and 30% for educational and industrial expenses. The Russian co-investors should receive a total of 799,587 yuan. A dividend of 300,000 yuan should be transferred to the province for verification and collection, and 100,000 yuan should be paid to the Yongheng Official Bank for transfer. A report should be submitted to the Provincial Government and letters sent to the Education and Agricultural and Mining Bureaus for verification. The remaining funds will be paid in installments in the second half of the year. The company's surplus in 1918 increased by over 400,000 yuan compared to 1917, mainly because the coal produced by the mine was able to be sold more easily due to the bombing of the Zha mine last year, resulting in higher profits. (May 31st)

Korean Residents Destroyed the Andong Customs 71

Andong Dispatch: In March of last year, the Andong Customs received instructions from the government to abolish the one-third land special tax on goods from Japan and to implement the new tariff regulations, under which all goods imported from Japan would be taxed according to the new tariff regulations. At that time, Japanese residents in Andong argued that the new tariff hindered trade with Japan and protested against it, but to no avail.

However, since then, some unscrupulous Japanese and Korean merchants have frequently secretly transported goods into Andong to evade customs duties for their own benefit. The Andong Customs has taken strict preventive measures and has uncovered numerous cases of tax evasion. Recently, another incident was discovered in which Korean residents evaded customs duties, gathered a crowd, rioted, and destroyed the customs office. The Andong Customs Commissioner has formally protested to the Japanese side. The events of the Korean residents' riot are as follows: Early in the morning of the 17th of this month, Korean merchants, including Park, secretly transported 17 boxes of rubber shoes worth approximately 18,000 Japanese yen from Sinuiju on the opposite shore by sailboat, hoping to evade customs duties. When they were transporting the rubber shoes to Liudaogou, just as they were about to land, a Customs officer patrolling the coast discovered them and rushed to the scene. He removed the rubber shoes from the boat. The Korean residents, unwilling to accept this, swarmed forward and engaged in hand-to-hand combat with the Customs officer. The Korean residents were outnumbered and fled. The Customs officer confiscated all of the rubber shoes in accordance with the regulations. Around 7:00 PM that evening, the Korean residents gathered over 200 accomplices from Sinuiju, armed with guns and clubs, and surrounded and destroyed all the doors and windows of the coastal customs office. Several Customs officers suffered minor injuries. Fortunately, Chinese police arrived and dispersed the rioters, saving the Customs officers from further harm. Although the Japanese police heard about the riot of the Korean residents, they were slow to arrive, seemingly condoning the riot. Subsequently, the Andong Customs Commissioner protested to the Japanese side. The Japanese police station, unable to refuse, arrested three or five Korean residents who participated in the riot and detained them for questioning. On the third day, a Korean resident's body was suddenly discovered on the riverbank. Based on this, the Japanese side protested to the Andong Customs, strongly claiming that the deceased was killed by a Customs officer. The Customs side pointed out that there was clear evidence that the deceased had fallen into the river and drowned. The two sides are currently negotiating, each holding its own position. It is difficult to predict how it will end. (May 27th)

Local Dispatches

Songjiang 72

Thugs Using Water Police to Extort Money: On the 11th of last month, Zhou A'gen, a farmer from the sixth map of Shanyangxiang, was returning from Shanghai after selling cattle. When he reached the Wang Huzi Bridge in Jiangzhuangzhen, thugs Zhu A'zhao, Lu A'jin, and Guan, claiming to be water police detectives, seized Zhou, accusing him of selling illegal substances. Zhou insisted that he was a law-abiding citizen who would never do anything illegal. However, Song and others refused to listen and searched him thoroughly. As a result, they found 53 silver dollars and 130 copper coins. Besides these, there was nothing else. They returned 10 silver dollars and ordered him to leave. Zhou felt aggrieved because the remaining 40 silver dollars were the proceeds from selling the cattle, which he intended to use to pay rent. He argued with them, but Song and others became angry out of shame and dragged Zhou to Tinglin and turned him over to the third squadron of the water police headquarters. Gong, the squadron leader, did not investigate and tortured Zhou, forcing him to confess (it is rumored that Song A'zhao and others are Gong's disciples). Later, because there was no evidence, Zhou was released on the 14th. Zhou, who had been unjustly detained and whose cattle money had been taken away, filed a complaint with the 16th district sub-office. District Chief Xu sent a letter of inquiry and demanded the return of the confiscated silver dollars. After many days of negotiation, the original silver dollars were returned on the 22nd, but Song A'zhao and others are still at large. The local people are very indignant about this.

Robbery and Injury in Huangqiao Town: The home of Xu Yada in Miaobang, 23rd map of Huangqiao Town, 10th district of the county, was suddenly robbed by more than ten bandits on the evening of the 31st of last month. The bandits, armed with knives and sticks, looted the house and forced the owner to reveal the location of the hidden silver. When this failed, the bandits beat and injured Xu. Yesterday (6th), Xu came to Songjiang to report the incident to the county government and request an examination. The examination revealed that Xu had two wounds from wooden objects and one knife wound. Instructions were given to investigate and arrest the bandits and punish them.

Suzhou 73

Li Cheng Cross-Appeal Trial Opens Before the Trial, State Premier Li Genyuan and his Third Concubine Cheng Peiyi Cross-Appeal Case: Cheng Peiyi, dissatisfied with the first instance judgment imposing a fine of fifteen yuan, filed an appeal. Yesterday (the 6th), the case was still heard by the local court. The trial opened at 2 p.m. Both parties appeared in person, and their respective defense lawyers Tang Shenfang and Zhu Fucheng appeared to defend them. After the trial opened, the judge announced an adjournment because the defendants Shi Ru, a monk, and Ma Shulan had not complied with the summons to appear in court. Shi Ru, a monk, and Ma Shulan must be brought to court, and the confession of Shi Ru, a monk, previously made to the West District Office of the Public Security Bureau, stating that he was ordered by Chief Li to persuade Cheng Peiyi to become a nun, must be retrieved before a new date for the trial is set.

Third Prison Uproar Continued: It was reported that at around 7 a.m. on the 5th, a riot of prisoners occurred in the third prison of Jiangsu on Siqian Street. Subsequently, thirty-three leading prisoners, including Du Junchen, were shackled and transferred to Nos. 4 and 18 in a ward. Yesterday (the 6th), Warden Lin and Chief Wang ordered the most important ones to be transferred to the third prison of Jiangsu in Xiaoliuzhen Lane, and the remaining accomplices were still imprisoned in the third prison. After the riot, each ward was sealed to prevent prisoners from moving freely outside the ward. Opening the seal required an order from the warden.

Woodworking Union Concerned About Domestic Goods: The Wuxian Woodworking Union recently experienced a strike, which has now subsided. Yesterday (the 6th), a meeting was held to propose: (1) Although the strike has ended, there are concerns that some employers may still deduct wages and disregard workers. It was resolved to send a letter to all employers stating that they must not deduct wages, maintain labor-management agreements, and persuade workers to be understanding and not to start disputes rashly. If an employer deducts wages, a report should be made to the union, and the union will negotiate with the employer based on reason. (2) Silk goods in this industry are sluggish and there are concerns that some employers may use this as an excuse to stop machines, which would affect the livelihoods of workers. It was resolved to send a letter to all employers stating that they must not use this as an excuse to stop machines in order to maintain the livelihood of workers. (3) The market is full of foreign goods, and silk goods in this industry have declined year after year. It was resolved to earnestly persuade all institutions and the public to use domestic goods to promote the industry.

County Government Approves Relocation: The county government is scheduled to relocate on the 15th of this month to the former site of the municipal government. Everything is currently being prepared. The Construction Bureau plans to reorganize streetlights. Because the streetlights in Wuxian are too dim and the installation is not entirely appropriate, the Wuxian Construction Bureau yesterday (the 6th) drafted measures to replace 40 to 200 streetlights. Roads that have been widened, such as Hulong Street and Jingde Road, will be equipped with streetlights in the center of the street, similar to Shanghai. The plan has been submitted to the county government for approval.

Fengxian 74

Land Survey of Roads in Mu: The land occupied by county roads in this county, from east to west, is approximately 52 li, with each li being approximately 9 mu and 9 fen, totaling more than 510 mu. Previously, former Director Wang proposed dividing the land into upper, middle, and lower grades, allocating a budget, and paying up to 60 yuan per mu, requiring a total of more than 31,000 yuan. The provincial government approved the decision to reimburse the amount over three years. However, it is now proposed to survey and allocate the grain tax on the road surface to each household, preparing for an exemption from payment during the upcoming spring tribute. Therefore, the current acting director, Zhou Jiuxu, has organized a surveying team to go to various places to survey and exempt the land according to the original land area, regardless of irregularities. The Finance Bureau has been requested to appoint a registrar to fill out the forms, with a deadline of the end of June.

Zhuanghang Joint Disaster Donation Report: The Zhuanghang joint disaster donation, including subsidies from both the provincial and national governments, totaled more than 40,000 yuan. Now that the post-disaster relief work in the town has been completed and the destroyed urban area has been restored, the post-disaster relief committee has prepared a report and accounting statement, and printed a separate booklet outlining the facts of the matter for public verification.

Qingpu 75

Repeated Robberies Throughout the Town: Shenxiang Town, located 20 li from the county seat, is on the border between Songjiang and Qingpu. Songjiang County has not dispatched a police station, and Qingpu County lacks adequate defense. Unexpectedly, on the afternoon of the 4th of this month, more than 40 bandits with two bandit ships and weapons looted the entire town, causing losses of several thousand yuan. Before leaving, they kidnapped five members of the wealthier Wu family. The local people were helpless and allowed them to search and loot. Only after the bandits had left did they report to the county government for arrest, but they had disappeared without a trace.

Capsized Boat Narrowly Avoids Disaster: A horse-drawn boat traveling from Zhujiajiao to Zhangliantang capsized yesterday afternoon at the Lianhe River estuary due to strong winds that broke the sail. The more than ten passengers all fell into the water. Fortunately, they grabbed onto the boat boards and were rescued by nearby villagers who heard their cries for help.

Education Bureau Plans to Borrow Emergency Funds: The education funds in this county have always been stretched thin. Because the summer vacation is approaching, the education funds for April, May, and June have not yet been secured. It is proposed to borrow 30,000 yuan in emergency funds to be used for summer vacation payments. This matter has been agreed upon by the local administrative authorities and submitted to the county administrative meeting for approval.

Defense Corps Clashes with the Public: The Beishan Defense Corps in this county clashed with the public the day before yesterday. The incident occurred because villagers were celebrating a deity in the Chenghuang Temple (commonly known as "making a society"). A large crowd of worshipers gathered like a wall. Unexpectedly, in the afternoon, more than ten troublemakers carried a statue into the defense corps headquarters (because the headquarters was originally located in the Chenghuang Temple). The defense corps members tried to stop them, but they were too aggressive. The corps commander ordered more than ten shots to be fired into the sky to stop them, but this incited the crowd, making the situation even more tense. Fortunately, the district party headquarters and the district office intervened and managed to resolve the matter. Subsequently, the district chief, Zhang Deru, and the corps commander, Lu Qi, reported to the county government. The county government immediately dispatched police to the countryside and arrested the thirteen ringleaders, who will be interrogated.

Wuxi 76

Three Thugs Rob a Lone Traveler: A man from Taizhou named A Ju has been operating a stall selling imported goods in Hongshengli, Wuyi. On the afternoon of the other day, A Ju was carrying more than 60 yuan in silver from the countryside to the city to buy goods when he was suddenly accosted by three thugs wearing short clothes and carrying guns near Yutang Bridge. The thugs robbed A Ju of all the silver he was carrying. A Ju, unable to resist, had to return home dejectedly.

Murdering Nun Arrested and Sent to County for Interrogation: Miaode, the abbess of the Shuiyue Nunnery in Dangkou Town, Nanyan City, was strangled to death on the evening of the 30th of last month by Wang Delin, a rogue monk from the area, during an attempted theft. The suspect was arrested by the seventh branch of the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, he was sent to the county for investigation. The criminal monk Wang Delin confessed that he saw the money and became greedy. He entered the nunnery at night with his face blackened with tin foil ash to scare and extort money. When he failed, he strangled Miaode to death with his belt. The investigation officer, Zhou Cheng, immediately ordered him to be shackled and imprisoned pending judgment.

County Rural Clearing Bureau Established: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs recently stated that although the lake bandits in Taihu Lake have been wiped out, the counties along the lake and nearby should actively clear the countryside. Therefore, it specially issued regulations for handling rural clearing, ordering eleven counties, including Wujiang, Wuxian, and Wuxi, to establish rural clearing bureaus as soon as possible to carry out rural clearing. County Magistrate Sun of this county has received the order and is preparing to establish the County Rural Clearing Bureau on the 16th of this month, with County Magistrate Sun concurrently serving as the bureau chief. The bureau will be located in the county government, and rural clearing sub-bureaus will be established in each district, with the district chief concurrently serving as the sub-bureau chief.

Resolutions of the First District: The First District Office of Xiyi has been located in the county government. Recently, District Chief Qian has been approved by the county government to relocate to the original site of the Municipal Preparatory Office. The seventh district affairs meeting was held the other day, and the following major cases were resolved: (1) How to raise funds for township offices and public projects. It was resolved that the district office should submit a report to the county government requesting instructions. (2) Opening slaughterhouses. It was resolved that the district office should plan a site. If there is suitable public open space in the township, the district office should be notified first for selection, and a concrete plan should be prepared and incorporated into the 19th-year administration plan and submitted to the county for review.

Gun Purchase Case Shrouded in Suspicion: On the morning of the 31st of last month, detectives from the county police brigade suddenly went to the Hongyusheng Rice Store on Guanqian Street and took away an assistant named Ding Fubao. For several days, he was neither interrogated nor transferred to the county. For a time, rumors spread on the street, but the truth remains unknown. The store is owned by Xing, whose son is currently a staff member of the County Government Social Investigation Office. According to him, after Ding Fubao was detained, his mother came to his house to borrow thirty yuan, but he refused because he could not afford it. She came to borrow every day for two days in a row, almost kneeling down and begging, but eventually left in disappointment. He (Xing himself) personally went to the brigade headquarters to visit Ding Fubao and saw that his face was pale and his limbs seemed to have been injured. He learned that a squad member from the Third Company had sold a pistol to someone else through Ding. The day after that, the brigade headquarters suddenly sent police to summon Xing to the team. The brigade commander personally asked him, saying that Ding Fubao had confessed that the pistol was indeed sold by him through Xing. Xing firmly denied it. At first, he was going to be detained, but because Xing was currently a county government staff member, he was released. According to Xing Zhongqing, the pistol was bought by someone from a sand camp. It is also rumored that Xing Cuqing and someone in the police team had a dispute over a woman, which led to this prison sentence. The truth is still difficult to ascertain.

Strictly Prohibit Setting Off Firecrackers: After midnight the other night, County Magistrate Sun suddenly heard the sound of gunfire in the distance and, fearing an accident, immediately sent the county police team to investigate. It was discovered that Huang Yuhu, the owner of Zhang Xiaoquan Scissor Shop, had set off firecrackers for a birthday celebration. Huang was taken into custody and slightly reprimanded before being released. Yesterday, the County Public Security Bureau issued a notice strictly prohibiting the setting off of firecrackers.

Changzhou 77

Two Robbery Cases Occur in the First District: Two robbery cases have recently occurred in the territory of the First District of Wuyi: (1) The home of Bai Qiaobao in Xicao Village, about five li from Baijia Bridge outside the East Gate, was robbed on the night of the 4th. Bai's eldest son was severely injured by being burned with kerosene. Silver and clothing were stolen. (2) The home of Chu Rongda in Chujia Xiaoqiaotou Village, Qinglong Township, was also robbed the night before. Rongda was stabbed in several places. The self-defense corps went to the rescue, and the thieves fled with the stolen goods.

Prosecutor Inspects Apprentice Suicide: Chang Junqing of Daixi Bridge in the Sixth District of Wuyi runs a stonemason shop. An apprentice named Xiaolong was mistreated by the shop owner's wife, Zhou. He suddenly committed suicide by jumping into the river on the evening of the 2nd. His body floated to the surface on the 3rd. The district chief, He Bingyi, reported the case to the county court prosecutor's office because it was a matter of life and death. He also handed over Zhou to the corps defense for supervision. Prosecutor Zhang went to the countryside to inspect the body on the evening of the 5th.

Nantong 78

Rear Hospital Organized: The Commander-in-Chief's Office plans to establish a rear hospital in Tongzhou, which has been determined to be located on Langshan Mountain. The headquarters sent the director of the military hospital to Tongzhou to discuss the matter with County Magistrate Zhang. A preparatory meeting was held at the General Chamber of Commerce on the 5th, and the work was divided into groups. Local doctors provided assistance, and nursing staff were hired by the county government.

Bandits Attack Qianshan Town at Night: A large group of bandits attacked Qianshan Town in Dongxiang on the nights of the 3rd and 4th. The bandits carried a large number of flashlights to illuminate the entire town. The police team and defense corps intercepted them, and the bandits resisted fiercely. The provincial police team stationed in Jinsha rushed to assist in the suppression. The bandits retreated only at dawn on the 5th.

Telegram Orders Interrogation of Captured Bandits: The Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui stated that the Tongyi Bandit Suppression Army killed more than 100 bandits from the pseudo-Red Army Fourteenth Army and captured more than 30 in the village of Huolong Town. County Magistrate Zhang was ordered by telegram to interrogate the captured bandits in detail, record their confessions, and submit them for review.

Three Bandit Leaders Executed: The special affairs team stationed in Jinsha arrested three notorious bandits in Dongxiang, nicknamed Haizhi, Yeying, and Caishen. The evidence was conclusive. After interrogation by military and police officers, they were executed on the spot.

Zhenjiang 79

Government Meeting to Comfort Wounded Soldiers: Because a large number of wounded soldiers have been transported to Zhenjiang in the past day or two, the Zhenjiang County Government held a meeting yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. at the Chamber of Commerce to discuss ways to comfort them. It was decided that because there were a large number of wounded soldiers, representatives from various organizations would gather at the County Party Headquarters and go to the No. 36 Standard Rear Hospital outside the South Gate to comfort them. The county government and the Provincial Public Security Bureau each contributed 50 yuan, the Chamber of Commerce 150 yuan, the Fortress Headquarters 20 yuan, and the Finance Bureau 30 yuan, for a total of 300 yuan. The county government and the Chamber of Commerce were tasked with purchasing beef and banana leaf fans to take to the wounded soldiers.

Second District Chief's Fraud Case Appealed: Zhang Ronggui, the former chief of the Second District of Zhenjiang County, colluded with Police Captain Cao to commit fraud. Wu Zhongzheng and others, residents of Gaozi Township, filed a lawsuit in the criminal court of the court. The prosecutor's office filed a public prosecution, and the civil court sentenced him to four months in prison with a two-year suspended sentence. It is now known that the plaintiffs, Wu Zhongzheng and others, are dissatisfied with the original verdict and have filed an appeal. The criminal court prosecutor also believes that the two-year suspended sentence is inappropriate and has also filed an appeal. The outcome remains to be seen.

Yangzhou 80

Hualong Bank Bankruptcy Liquidation: It has recently been heard that the financial community in Yangzhou has been greatly affected since the bankruptcy of Yongji and Hengyan. The number of money houses that have closed down includes three major ones, of which Hualong's deficit is the largest, shorting 130,000 yuan in the various Zhuang and Branch Numbers in Su, Shen, and Zhen. Representatives from the Zhuang and Branch Numbers from various locations have been dispatched to Yangzhou to negotiate. Huang Yizhi and Pan Songping and others from the money industry here have come out to mediate. This morning (5th) at 10 a.m., the third mediation meeting was held at the Chamber of Commerce. After repeated exchanges of opinions, the meeting had not dispersed by 2 p.m. It is said that Hualong only agreed to hand over 70,000 yuan for amortization, while the creditors demanded that it reach more than 70%. Therefore, there is a difference of more than 20,000 yuan, so

Mediation is still not easy. As for the remaining more than 50,000 yuan owed to the various Zhuang households in this city, there is a way to resolve it only after Su Shen Zhen settles it.

Gaoyou 81

Gaoyou Police Captain Appointed: The position of police captain of this county was originally held concurrently by the county magistrate. Now, Man Shi Du has been specially appointed by the Department of Civil Affairs and arrived in the mail on the evening of the 3rd. However, the date for taking over has not yet been set.

Tragic News in a Year of Famine: Pan Dekui, a farmer from Manyang Village in this county, and his family of seven depended entirely on the meager ten or so mu of land inherited from his ancestors for a living. Unexpectedly, last year's famine resulted in no harvest. In addition, rice and firewood have become expensive recently, and they have no money to buy rice. They had no choice but to go to the fields to dig up reed roots to eat, and they have been doing so for half a month with no other abnormalities. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, after eating, they all felt numbness throughout their bodies and abdominal pain. They died one after another, which is truly tragic.

Pinghu 82

Robbery Occurs in Longyang: The homes of two farmers, Xu Chunbo and Xu Jiafu, in Longyang, about four li from Xincang, were suddenly attacked on the night of the 2nd by more than ten bandits carrying guns and knives who broke down the doors and ransacked the homes. They bound Chunbo, hung him up, and beat him, forcing him to reveal the location of the silver. They also beat a worker named Jia. In the end, they robbed them of more than 100 yuan in silver and clothes and jewelry, causing losses of about 400 to 500 yuan to the two families. The bandits fired their guns as a warning before leaving, heading east.

Arrested Thief Handed Over to County Government: Wang Ah Hu, a member of the bandit gang from Nan Zhang Shaqiao, had been hiding elsewhere for a long time and had not been arrested. The other night, he was sleeping in a boat moored in a remote place when detectives from the Xincang Public Security Branch discovered him and led armed police officers to arrest him. Ah Hu was unable to escape while sleeping and was arrested. He was handed over to the county for prosecution by Branch Chief Shen yesterday.

Huzhou 83

Dong Jun'e Flees from His Post: Dong Jun'e, the chief of the Zhili Public Security Branch in Wuxing, recently arrested the accountant of the Yuanchang Cocoon Company in the town without authorization, which caused all the shops in the town to strike and attack the county magistrate. He arrived at the town on the 2nd of this month and has confirmed the facts. On this day, a police officer drowned, Shen Chengbao. Therefore, County Magistrate Gong took Dong to Huzhou and temporarily detained him in the detention center of the Wuxing Public Security Bureau. Unexpectedly, Dong Jun'e suddenly escaped early yesterday morning. Fang Xiaokuan, the acting chief of the Liyi County Public Security Bureau, immediately sent police officers to search for him in all directions. By noon, there was no sign of him. Dong's family is still in Zhili, so Chief Fang has telegraphed the Zhili Public Security Bureau to quickly detain Dong's family and send a telegram to all counties and major towns to assist in the arrest.

Road Construction Foreman Robbed by Bandits: The road construction foreman on the Three Heavens Gate section of the Hangzhou-Changxing Highway was robbed by bandits yesterday morning when he went to the Huzhou Bureau to collect his wages. When he was passing Yangjiabu, just one li from Three Heavens Gate, two bandits suddenly emerged from the grass and demanded that he stop the sedan and search for opium. The sedan carriers saw that the two bandits each had a pistol and had no choice but to stop and allow the bandits to search. The bandits robbed the foreman of 105 yuan in silver that he had in his pocket. After the incident, the foreman went to Three Heavens Gate and led dozens of road workers to the grass where the bandits had been, but there was no one there.

Account of the Collapse of Tongkang Zhuang: The Ningbo Xiaotonghang Tongkang Money House collapsed this time at the same time as the Gengyu Zhuang due to shareholder He Gengxing's deficit. Kidnapped and Looted: Shi Mou, the owner of Shi Shenghuo Wine House in the Liangqiao area of ​​southern Yuyao, was kidnapped last year and redeemed for 2,000 yuan. Five robbers suddenly broke into his house at one o'clock the other night. Three of them rushed in to rob, and two guarded the door.

Xiaoshan 85

Traces of Non-Ferrous Metal Mines Discovered in Tianzhao Mountain: Tianzhao Mountain, near Yiqiao Xinba in Xiaoshan, was previously sought to be purchased several times by French merchants. Because the residents thought that it would hinder the land, they refused. Now, an owner who purchased it excavated to a depth of one foot the other day. It is all stone and rock without thick soil, and the exposed stone is bright and visible. After observation by the reporters, it is said that it is a non-ferrous metal mine.

Farmers' Movement in Beiqian Mountain Resolved: Du Shihua, the head of Xiaoshan County, ordered that more than 50 mu of farmland in Beiqian Mountain be used as an agricultural experimental site. The tenants there were unwilling to give way, resulting in a farmers' movement. Finally, Wang Xiufu, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, repeatedly persuaded them to agree to take back the land rights from the tenants for 30 yuan per mu and establish a contract to resolve the farmers' movement.

Peng Weixun Case Brought to Public Prosecution: Peng Weixun, the director of the Yiqiao Public Security Branch in Xiaoshan, was found to have committed a crime in the case of unauthorized punishment of the absconding case by the county court prosecutor's office, and the county government was requested to suspend the director of the Public Security Branch and return him to the case for investigation. Then, because Peng Weixun brought gambling equipment to Hangzhou, he was seized by the Provincial Public Security Bureau and sent to the Ministry of Civil Affairs, which was issued to Xiaoshan County by the court for joint trial. After the investigation by the prosecutor's office of the county court, it was believed that Peng Weixun had indeed committed the crime of defrauding property and filed a public prosecution in accordance with the law.

Old Calendar

Festivals Calculated Using the National Calendar 92

Announced by the Municipal Government Yesterday

The Municipal Government issued a notice yesterday stating that the Ministry of Education's advice was approved. The table of holidays for various agencies and schools has been announced and implemented. However, only a small number of members of the general public are subject to a weekly rest system. The original rest opportunities, such as various festivals in the old calendar, have also been eliminated since the abolition of the old calendar. It seems that they are busy working all year round and do not stipulate certain rest and entertainment dates within a considerable period of time to adjust their lives. They feel too boring and cannot increase the efficiency of their work. After consultation with the Ministry, it was proposed to formulate appropriate alternative measures after the abolition of the old calendar festivals and submit them to the Executive Yuan to be forwarded to the National Government for review. Now, the Executive Yuan's Order No. 1314 was received, stating that the Ministry reported that all the old calendar festivals should be abolished and alternative festivals should be set up for the people to rest and entertain. After copying the original signature, it was ordered to comply with the handling, etc., and copied the original signature and sent it to the Ministry. It should be complied with after copying and sending the original to the Ministry, and incorporated into the National Calendar of the Republic of China in the 20th year, and announced in conjunction with the distribution order, the corresponding original was copied and sent to the Ministry and the Office of Civil Servants to check and announce that all old calendar festivals should be calculated using the national calendar. January 1 of the national calendar should be New Year's Day, the 15th should be Shangyuan, March 3 should be the Xichen, May 5 should be Chongwu, July 15 should be Zhongyuan, September 9 should be Chongjiu, December 8 should be Laba, and the Mid-Autumn Festival should be changed to the closest day to the Autumnal Equinox. The earliest is September 9 and the latest is October 7. The customs of watching lanterns, repairing Xichen, racing, worshipping ancestors, enjoying the moon, and climbing high for entertainment and rest that the people have been using in the old calendar shall be held at any time in accordance with the national calendar, so that the people's excessive labor can be adjusted. All agencies and schools should still follow the announced table of holidays for various agencies and schools as the standard for their holidays, and it is hoped that they will still order their subordinates to announce and implement them.

Extended for Another Six Months 93

Calculated from May 18, 19th year. The Shanghai Garrison Headquarters received an order from the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs to forward the Executive Yuan's instructions. Municipal Government Eliminates Feudal Remnants 102

Orders Police to Confiscate and Burn Temple Imperial Tablets

The various temples and monasteries in the city often have tablets inscribed with "Long Live the Emperor" enshrined in the main halls. The municipal government considers this kind of outdated custom to be a tool for flattery during the autocratic era. Now that the imperial system has long been overthrown and the national system has been changed to a republic, all feudal remnants should be eliminated by the current government in order to sweep away the dust and create a new citizenry. Yesterday, a special order was issued to the Public Security Bureau to instruct its subordinates to investigate, confiscate, and destroy such tablets in order to conform to the political system.

Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee

Explains Method of Electing Representatives 108

Must be elected according to law ten days in advance. The Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee is scheduled to convene a meeting of member representatives from all industry guilds in the city on the 21st of this month to formally establish the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The committee has now sent letters to each guild to quickly elect representatives. However, there are many who do not understand the method of calculating the number of representatives and the number of employees. The Secretariat has provided a detailed explanation as follows:

(1) Method of calculating the number of representatives and the number of employees. Each guild may elect one representative, but if the average number of employees in each store belonging to the guild (because the number of employees in the store may be different in the first and second half of the year or each month, so the average number should be obtained) exceeds fifteen, then for every fifteen people exceeding that number, one additional representative may be added, but the maximum should not exceed twenty-one. This method allows guilds with more employees to have a corresponding increase in the number of representatives in the chamber of commerce. This is very different from the previous chamber of commerce, where each guild often only elected one or two people as members of the chamber of commerce, which often led to the affairs of the chamber of commerce being monopolized by one or two people. Therefore, the number of representatives elected by the guilds to attend the chamber of commerce this time should be increased as much as possible, and it should not be like the previous practice of only one or two people per guild. As far as the burden of membership fees is concerned, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously charged 100 yuan for each additional member, but now it has been reduced to 50 yuan. Therefore, based on the amount of membership fees paid, those who could only elect two people in the past can now elect four people. The number of employees should be calculated based on the total number of employees in each store belonging to the guild, not the clerks and employees employed by the guild itself. This point should be especially clear.

(2) Method of electing representatives. The representatives elected by the members of the guild should be recommended by the executive committee of the guild and given a letter of authorization to notify the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee. If the guild's internal structure has not been reorganized in accordance with the law and the old board of directors system is still used, then it should be recommended by the board of directors. The industry group reorganization committee should be recommended by the reorganization committee. When the guilds elect more than one representative, they should also be elected from stores with a larger number of employees. This is stipulated in the detailed rules for the implementation of the Chamber of Commerce Law. The representatives of companies or stores should be recommended by the board of directors or shareholders and managers. (3) Membership of stores. According to the Chamber of Commerce Law, stores may join the Chamber of Commerce as store members independently only if there is no same industry in the city, or if there is a same industry but there is no organization of the same industry guild. However, there are still the following two methods for store members in this city: (A) If there is a same industry guild but the guild has not registered with the Chamber of Commerce, or if it has registered but has not accepted guidance and reorganization, it should still be considered as having no same industry guild, and the stores in that industry may still join the Chamber of Commerce as store members independently. (B) Organizations of more than one industry, such as the Chinese Cotton Mill Federation, the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Mill Cocoon Industry General Association, and the Jiangsu Match Federation, are fundamentally inconsistent with the Industrial and Commercial Industry Guild Law, so they should also be considered as having no same industry guild, and their members may still join the Chamber of Commerce independently. The number of representatives elected by store members is stipulated by the Chamber of Commerce Law to be from one to three.

Page 14

(4) Qualifications of member representatives. Regardless of whether it is a guild or a store, the representatives they elect must be citizens of the Republic of China who are engaged in commerce in this region and are over 25 years of age. Those who have any of the following circumstances may not serve as representatives: (A) Those who have been deprived of civil rights and have not yet had them restored. (B) Those who have engaged in counter-revolutionary activities and have been convicted by a court. (C) Those who have been declared bankrupt and have not yet had their rights restored, or those who have engaged in commerce and have become insolvent or bankrupt and have not yet restored their credit. (D) Those who lack the capacity to act, that is, those who have not reached the legal age and are mentally deficient as stipulated in the current General Principles of the Civil Code.

(5) Membership fees to be paid by representatives. The basic membership fees to be paid by each guild or store must be determined by the general meeting of members, so they cannot be collected yet. However, the attendance fees for representatives have been approved by the Social Bureau and submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for record. The amount of collection is as follows: (A) Guild representatives will be charged an attendance fee of 50 yuan per person, plus 15 yuan for repaying construction public bonds, for a total of 65 yuan. (B) Store representatives will be charged an attendance fee of 30 yuan per person, plus 9 yuan for repaying construction public bonds, for a total of 39 yuan. The above attendance fees should be paid together with the notification of the recommended representative to the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee.

(6) Deadline for electing representatives. According to the resolution of the plenary meeting of the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee, the representatives should be elected by the 10th of this month because the committee still has various preparatory procedures to be completed after the representatives of each industry have been elected, which may be too late.

Silk Factory Industry

Guild Holds Committee Meeting Yesterday 111

The Shanghai Silk Factory Industry Guild convened a committee meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday. The executive committee members who attended included Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Jingan, Shen Huachen, Huang Jinfan, Zhang Yunsheng, and Zhang Peishen. Shen Huachen chaired the meeting as usual, and six important cases were resolved: (1) It was discussed that the Zhejiang Railway lacked freight cars for transporting cocoons, causing the cocoons waiting to be transported to pile up at the station, resulting in huge losses due to sun and rain. It was resolved to telegraph the Zhejiang Provincial Government to negotiate with the Railway Bureau to allocate more freight cars for quick transportation. (2) It was discussed that the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee sent a letter stating that a meeting of representatives of the industry guilds would be held on June 21 and requesting the election of representatives to attend. It was resolved that all members of the committee would attend. (3) It was discussed that the market price of silk for export was still sluggish, while the cost of cocoons was very high, making the future dangerous. Workers in the Japanese silk and cotton industries voluntarily reduced their salaries by 20%. China, with its rising cost of living, must take both into consideration. It was resolved that the treatment of employees and female workers would be maintained for the time being. If it becomes absolutely necessary, it will be discussed further. The festival awards for female workers will be issued from June onwards according to the previous year's practice. (4) It was discussed that the Social Bureau sent a letter inquiring about the silk factory industry's habit of paying employees double salaries at the end of the year. The consensus was that double salaries at the end of the year were a special reward from the factory, which was customary but not legally mandated. Some factories paid them at the end of the year, while others did not, because they were actually suffering losses. Those who had informed the guild in advance that they would not pay were communicating mutual understanding. It was resolved to reply truthfully. (5) It was discussed that the previous request to the government to abolish the three-part form for transporting cocoons and to exempt them from the inland transit tax. The Ministry of Finance replied that according to the Chief Inspector of Customs, the Shanghai Customs did not require the use of the three-part form for purchasing cocoons. The request to order the customs to abolish the three-part form should not be considered. Foreign merchants, according to the treaty, do not pay inland taxes when purchasing cocoons. Therefore, they use the three-part form to pay the inland transit tax. Now, Chinese merchants pay local taxes and should naturally be able to pass through with tax receipts and should not use the three-part form or imitate the payment of the inland transit tax. It was resolved to ask the Silk Cocoon General Association to investigate the case and reapply to the government for clear regulations to be followed. (6) It was discussed that the Silk Cocoon General Association previously discussed the new method of adding a stamp to the sales order for raw silk and that the guarantee form prepared by the Export Silk Guild when manufacturers sell silk should be in both Chinese and Western languages. It was resolved to ask the Silk Cocoon General Association to proceed according to the discussion. The meeting adjourned. (Appendix: Telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government) Chairman Zhang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, the spring cocoons in Zhejiang Province are being transported to Shanghai in full swing, but the Railway Bureau cannot allocate more freight cars, causing them to pile up at various stations along the Shanghai-Hangzhou line. Because the cocoons in these areas are close to the road and related to silk reeling, they are not dried sufficiently. Now, without vehicles for rapid transportation, they are piling up on the platforms and are prone to mold and rot from sun and rain. Some have already suffered irreparable losses. Please, Your Excellency, take into account the difficulties of the merchants, which are related to their capital, and immediately request the Railway Bureau to urgently increase the number of freight cars to facilitate the quick transportation of cocoons stored at various stations. We are extremely grateful. Shen Huachen, Chairman of the Shanghai Special City Silk Factory Industry Guild Committee, bows in song.

Postal Workers' Two Unions

Demand Abolition of Parcel Tax 114

The parcel tax began in 1927, and its tax rate is 2.5%, but it is actually more than 5%. It is said that Shanghai and Peiping are the two places with the highest revenue from this tax. The revenue from the parcel tax in Shanghai was approximately 600,000 yuan in the previous year, and it is said to have been approximately 1.2 million yuan last year. Because this tax rate greatly affects people's lives, before the National Tariff Reduction Conference is convened, postal workers, feeling the severity of this tax, have jointly requested the Ministry of Communications to abolish this tax rate.

However, the County Magistrate Fang Li, who previously agreed with the demolition, suddenly changed his attitude and deceitfully presented to the Department of Civil Affairs that the pagoda was swaying in the wind and attached an opinion proposing to demolish it and erect a small stele with the inscription "Bao Xing Pagoda" and other words. The local gentry, upon learning of this, were surprised that the County Magistrate, as an official of the revolutionary government, should be fair and truthful, but instead used deceitful words to deceive his superiors. Police Sergeants

Add Copper Numbers to Collar Patches 118

In order to facilitate inspection of police sergeant discipline and diligence,

The Municipal Public Security Bureau submitted a special report to the municipal government for record yesterday regarding the addition of copper numbers to the police sergeant collar patches. The report stated that Article 8 of the revised police uniform regulations issued by the Ministry of Interior stated that the police sergeant collar patches should have the place name on the left and the bureau name on the right, using copper material. Article 9 stated that the police sergeant lapel badges should indicate the position, name, and number for easy inspection. However, the lapel badge is worn on the left chest pocket, with only the upper end exposed, making it difficult to identify the position, name, and number. If a police sergeant exceeds his authority while on duty, the public often has no way to report it because they do not know his name and number. The lapel badge is 3 inches high and 2.5 inches wide, and the capacity for characters is limited, making it difficult to see clearly without detailed inspection, and the writing is easily blurred over time. Therefore, it is necessary to improve and change it. It is now proposed to add copper numbers to the police sergeant collar patches, with the place name and district on the left and the copper number on the right. They are divided into three types: patrol sergeant, patrol officer, and petition officer, all numbered sequentially from number one. The patrol sergeant collar patch will have the words "patrol sergeant" added before the number, the petition officer collar patch will have the word "petition" added before the number, and the regular patrol officer will only have the number without the words "patrol officer." This change is neither in violation of the regulations nor obviously marked, and it is also more convenient for inspecting police sergeant discipline and diligence. It is reported that the municipal government has already issued an order to approve it for record.

Crisis in Chinese Cigarette Industry 119

Emergency Meeting Held Yesterday

Petition to Beijing for Relief

Since last year, the Chinese cigarette industry has been in dire straits. Even large companies such as Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company have stopped production for reorganization. As of now, no fewer than a dozen large and small companies have continued to stop production. In March, they requested the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee to report to the government for relief. It is now learned that the industry is facing an inability to maintain itself due to the continuous sharp decline in foreign exchange rates. Therefore, an emergency meeting of all members was convened yesterday. The number of attendees was unusually high. Chairman Wu Tingsheng reported the purpose of the meeting, and the members described various painful situations, some with tears in their eyes. The main point was that the cost of raw materials was increasing daily due to the impact of foreign exchange rates, while the selling price was limited by tax levels, making it difficult to stop. Representatives from the Municipal Citizen Training Committee were greatly moved when they learned of the situation. As a result, it was resolved to petition Beijing for relief. The original plan was for all members to go, but after the Municipal Citizen Training Committee representatives explained that the number of people was not an issue, it was decided to form a petition group. Wu Tingsheng, Lao Jingxiu, Shen Xingde, Bao Gengsheng, Yao Jixian, Fan Songzhou, Weng Guangtian, and others were elected as representatives to carry out the petition to Beijing. It was also resolved to ask the Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee to send personnel to lead and the Municipal Party Department to provide assistance. They will depart as soon as the procedures are completed.

National Medical Association

Request to Postpone the Promulgation of the Provisional Regulations for Physicians 121

The National Medical Association, due to the fact that the (Provisional Regulations for Physicians) promulgated by the Ministry of Health for the first time were not in line with current needs, convened a national medical representative conference in November of last year, with over forty organizations from seventeen provinces participating in joint discussions. They unanimously decided to support the Central Health Commission's Decision No. 15, requesting the Ministry of Health to relax the registration qualifications for the first batch of physicians and sending representatives to Beijing to present their case in person. The Ministry of Health adopted their suggestions and submitted the revised regulations to the Legislative Yuan for review. Now, the revised regulations have been passed by the Legislative Yuan in its 88th meeting (the revised regulations were published in various newspapers on May 11). However, regarding articles 1, 2, 5, 15, etc. in the regulations, various medical associations have sent letters to the National Medical Association, believing that there are still difficulties in implementation. The Association's fifth executive committee meeting decided to draft a telegram to the Ministry of Health requesting a temporary postponement of the promulgation and implementation. The telegram issued by the Association yesterday is reproduced below: To Minister Liu of the Ministry of Health: Reports indicate that the Provisional Regulations for Physicians passed by the Legislative Yuan are dissimilar to the initial promulgation and also greatly different from the revised draft shown by the Medical Administration Department of your ministry on December 16 last year. There are many points that are difficult to implement, causing widespread confusion and complaints. This association has received letters from medical associations in various places, offering contributions on articles 1, 2, 5, and 15. We plan to compile these opinions and submit them to you in the coming days. We earnestly request a temporary postponement of promulgation and implementation. Furthermore, the full text passed by the Legislative Yuan this time is vastly different from the draft submitted by your ministry to the Yuan. We do not know whether it was modified on the spot by the Legislative Yuan or whether your ministry re-drafted a second draft. We hope for your guidance. Respectfully, Chairman Xu Naili of the National Medical Association.

Local News Two

Beggars Killing Each Other by the Bridge 124

For One Copper Coin

Little Ningbo Dies Bitterly

Bridge rickshaw pulling is a new invention by beggars in recent years, one of their methods of begging for money. Because there are many child beggars at each bridge, strict rules are set: if a vehicle (limited to rickshaws and charter cars) passes, if Beggar A greets it first, then Beggar B cannot compete to avoid competition. But on the afternoon of the 29th of last month, a rickshaw came onto the Garbage Bridge. The child beggar named Little Ningbo greeted it first, but his business was snatched away by a beggar named Wang Agen, and the one copper coin thrown by the passenger was taken by Wang. Little Ningbo, with the weak being prey to the strong, was unwilling, and thus they fought each other. Under fists and feet, Little Ningbo was injured internally and fell to the ground, dying shortly after. The police arrested the murderous beggar Wang Agen and another beggar Wang Zirong and took them to the police station, and reported the case to the magistrate to inspect the body and order its burial. Yesterday, they were sent to the Special District Local Court. Wang Zirong testified about the circumstances of the incident. Judge Wu concluded the interrogation and sentenced Wang Agen to four years of imprisonment. Wang Zirong was released to continue his life as a beggar.

Already Publicly Prosecuted

Case of Burying a Boy Alive 125

Hou Genbao Denies Everything

The Facts of the Case Await Investigation

Guan Maoda, Thirteen-Year-Old Son of Guan Liukun of Guan Lane, Tanziwan, Zhabei, Was Buried Alive on April 8th. It was later discovered that his maternal nephew, Hou Genbao, committed the crime due to an affair with his daughter, Guan Caidi, and to seize property. The Fourth District Police Station arrested Hou Genbao, while Guan Caidi fled. The case was handed over to the Local Court for investigation and public prosecution was initiated. Judge Deng held a court hearing yesterday. Hou Genbao claimed, "I am being wronged." The judge asked, "Why did you confess at the Fourth District Police Station?" (Answer) "I was tortured." (Question) "Why did you confess again at the Public Security Bureau?" (Answer) "They taught me to say that, and I dared not refuse for fear of torture." (Question) "Why did you run away?" (Answer) "On the ninth day, my maternal uncle told me to look for my cousin, and I wasn't running away. Later, I heard that I was involved, so I surrendered to the police station." Guan Liukun testified, "Mao Da is my son, and Cai Di is my daughter, but they were born to two different wives. Hou Genbao is the son of my younger sister, Hou Guan. Cai Di was not betrothed to Genbao. Mao Da was taken out to catch frogs by Hou Genbao at 1:00 PM on the eighth day. Around 3:00 PM, Genbao returned alone, supposedly to dig bamboo shoots for me. Later, after my son went missing, Genbao claimed to be searching for him on my behalf. After the body was discovered, his mother said that on the fourth day, Genbao dug a hole next to Tianshan. When his mother asked him, he said it was to bury a large crock. Unexpectedly, he pushed my son into the hole and buried him alive." The judge asked, "Besides his mother, is there anyone else who can testify to this matter?" (Answer) "No." At this point, Hou Guan testified, "I never said that my son dug a hole in advance. Because after Mao Da went missing, I also helped to search. I saw new soil next to the tomb, so I dug it up and saw a foot, which aroused my suspicion. After digging completely, I saw Mao Da's body, so I called Liukun to come and see." Patrolman Shi Zhaoyu testified that Hou Genbao was caught by them and did not surrender himself. When asked, the local guarantor Hou Shuren said that he knew nothing about the inside story before or after the event. Since the case still needs to be investigated, the judge ordered no debate to be opened, and the defendant was remanded in custody to await a rescheduled trial, and then adjourned the court.

Gold-Inlaid Jade Ring 126

Shanghai is Full of Swindlers

A Country Woman Almost Falls for a Scam

A country woman, Zhang Xu, accidentally visited Shanghai and fell victim to a scam. The woman was walking on Lan Road the other evening when she noticed three people on the left side of the road examining jewelry. One was the seller, and the other two were buyers. The seller took out a jade ring, saying that it was worth a lot but he needed money urgently, so he was only selling it for four taels of gold. The two buyers both wanted to buy it but complained that the price was too high and were still commenting. The country woman also stepped forward to play with it. The seller eagerly urged her to buy it, and the other two buyers also encouraged her, persuading the seller to lower the price. However, the country woman had no money on her, but her young daughter who was traveling with her had one tael of gold and an umbrella. The seller said that he urgently needed money, and although one tael of gold was too low, he was willing to sell it if she added the umbrella. After the woman made the deal and examined the ring carefully, she realized that it was not a gold-inlaid jade ring, but a counterfeit. Those people had not gone far, and she called out to Chinese Constable No. 1287, who apprehended Wang Changgen, a Ningbo native who was selling the ring, and took him to the Yangshupu Police Station. Unexpectedly, Wang Sanda and Wang Asan, two accomplices from Wuxi who were pretending to be buyers, went to the entrance of the police station to spy on the situation. Zhang Xu recognized them as the accomplices when she and Chinese Constable No. 1287 came out of the police station, so she had the two Wangs arrested as well. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Feng interrogated them. The three admitted to the deception and claimed that the fake jewelry was bought from the City God Temple for only thirty cents. Judge Feng, after verifying the confessions, sentenced Wang Changgen and the other two to six months of imprisonment each. The fake jade ring was confiscated, and the one silver dollar and one umbrella were returned to the original owner to claim.

Port Authority

News of the Reception of Nanshi Wharf 128

Payment can be made in mid-month. The Municipal Government Port Authority previously intended to develop the city's port plan by taking over the Dada and Datong wharves in Nanshi and then designating them for lease to various Chinese shipping companies to achieve unification. This matter was previously reported in this newspaper. Now, it is learned that the negotiations between the Port Authority and Dada and Datong regarding the takeover procedures have been settled, and the Chinese shipping companies leasing the wharves have also followed the Port Authority's order to pay a deposit of 700,000 yuan. On April 15th, they had already paid the first installment, which was one-tenth, or 70,000 yuan. Now, the Port Authority has notified the companies to continue to raise the second installment of the deposit before the 15th of this month, which is required to be five-tenths. Dada Company has a total of nine wharves, while Datong Company has a total of four wharves. Because the Port Authority is eager to take over, it plans to first pay 290,000 yuan from this second installment to the two companies, with 110,000 yuan going to Datong and 180,000 yuan going to Dada. The remaining wharf compensation will be paid when the third installment of the deposit is received. It has also been agreed that after collecting the second installment of the deposit, a draft contract for leasing the wharves will be signed with each shipping company.

Xi Zutong's Sentence for False Accusation 131

Six Crimes Combined, Six Years Imprisonment

Xi Declares He Will Appeal

Xi Zutong, the former executive committee member and organization minister of the Provisional Party Department of Nanhui County, falsely accused six loyal comrades of being communists during the purge in 1927. The victims sued Xi Zutong for false accusation and fraud in the Local Court. After public prosecution was initiated, after repeated trials, it was determined that the debate had ended. The judgment was pronounced by Judge Qian and Prosecutor Lei et al. the day before yesterday. Xi Zutong was sentenced to one year and ten months of imprisonment for each of the six counts of false accusation for obstructing the National Revolution, to be served concurrently for five years. The rest was acquitted. Xi Zutong declared in court that he did not accept the judgment. The judge ordered an appeal according to law and ordered him to be taken back into custody.

Datong Music Association

Revising the Zhonghe Shaole 134

Eight Timbres Complete

Among our country's music, the oldest and most valuable is none other than Zhonghe Shaole. Confucius praised it as perfect and complete, and even said that after hearing the Shao in Qi, he did not know the taste of meat for three months. Qin Shihuang burned books and buried scholars, destroying rites and music, but Shao alone survived. Dynasties past have placed great importance on its function, which can improve the atmosphere, eliminate violence, and avert disasters in the unseen world, bringing heavenly blessings from above and harmonizing the people's will below. Although the early Qing also intended to revise it, there were many inaccuracies in the music laws and palace scores, making it difficult to revive the true essence of the country's music. Since the creation of the new national grand music, the Datong Music Association of this port has repeatedly participated in national diplomacy, and Westerners who have heard it have praised it, recognizing the correct path of national music. Now, to take it to the next level, the revised Zhonghe Shaole score will adopt the new system, and all ordinary silk and bamboo instruments will also be added to increase the prevalence. Now, all procedures have been fully prepared, and practice can begin next Sunday.

Shanghai Bank Offers Small Credit Loans 136

Pilot Program to be Launched on Jing'an Temple Road

The Shanghai Bank has always been dedicated to serving society. Recognizing that small businesses and those who rely on savings for living have no financing options when they encounter financial difficulties, the bank is launching a pilot program for revolving small credit loans at its Jing'an Temple Road branch, modeled after the Morris Plan Bank system in the United States. This will provide financial assistance to those with stable employment and legitimate needs. It is reported that the interest rate is 1% per annum, and the monthly repayment is calculated by the bank at an annual interest rate of 4%. This approach is unprecedented in the Chinese banking industry and demonstrates the bank's commitment to adjusting civilian finances.

Descendants of Zhou Fuju

Accused of Not Returning Pawned Items 139

Liquidation of Wuchangtang Property

Borrowers File a Lawsuit

Zhou Zitian, a descendant of the late salt merchant Zhou Fuju, pawned the title deeds of 1,200 mu of land in the Dayu Company, Lihetai household, in Juegang, Nantong, 720 shares of the Pulisha Factory Zhou Zhiji and Zhou Xinji, and the title deeds of 1,200 mu of land in the Xinfuxiang household of the Dayu Company to Deyu Company, Nikkyoji Company, and Zhenyujunji Firm in September of the year before last, borrowing 67,000 taels of silver. Zhou Zishan guaranteed the loan with the property of Zhou Wuchangtang. The loan term was six months with an interest rate of 11 taels per month per thousand taels. When the term expired, Zitian did not redeem the items. The managers of the three pledgees hired lawyers to file a lawsuit, requesting the court to order the two Zhous to jointly repay the loan. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenyong of the Special District Local Court held a hearing, but the defendants did not appear. The plaintiff's lawyer presented evidence, and the defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant fully admitted to the loan, but the property of Wuchangtang was jointly owned by five branches, and Zishan was only managing it on their behalf. The property is currently being liquidated and its assets are being verified. Although there are more than one million yuan in assets, after deducting debts of 600,000 to 700,000, there is little left. However, the creditor's rights will not be lost. After the plaintiff filed the lawsuit, Wang Wenmei was sent to register at the Zhou Wuchangtang liquidation office, and the creditor also attended the meeting. This shows that the plaintiff has acknowledged the liquidation by the liquidation office, so the case should be suspended. However, according to Wang Wenmei, who attended the court, he went to inquire about the Zhou Wuchangtang liquidation advertisement because he was a middleman in the loan and was not commissioned by the plaintiff. After the lawyers for both parties finished their arguments, Judge Xu ordered the parties to wait until the morning of June 11 for the judgment.

Mother Sues Daughter to Recover Separated Property

Judge Orders Both Parties to Reconcile Outside of Court

Hou Liu, a local woman residing in Tanjia Ferry in the northwest township of this county, recently hired lawyer Wang Chengkuan to sue her biological daughter Jinjie (i.e., Jin Jinjie) in the Local Court for being unstable and remarrying after her husband's death. She requested to recover the divided property. Her statement was roughly as follows: The plaintiff is 66 years old this year and has no sons, only one daughter, the defendant Jinjie. When her first husband was alive, he raised a son named Xiaomao. She also recruited a son-in-law, Shen Agao, for the defendant. The defendant gave birth to a daughter, Yueying. In April of the Republic of China, because the son and the defendant had both grown up, she divided her late husband's property to Xiaomao (i.e., Hou Xiaomao, two mu, three fen, and nine li of land), and the defendant inherited two mu, four fen, three li, and one hao of land. All the houses were divided equally between Xiaomao and the defendant, and a contract was established. The plaintiff's food and clothing were to be provided by the defendant, and the plaintiff's aunt (who is currently 83 years old and still alive) was to be supported by the son, Hou Xiaomao. Unexpectedly, the son-in-law (i.e., the defendant's husband) Shen Agao died of illness in 1917. The defendant was unstable and had an affair with Jin Asan (i.e., Yinshan), and went out and seized the property without returning it. Later, due to lack of food and clothing, she forcibly moved back, and she and her subsequent husband abused the plaintiff. Last year, when the Shanghai Special Municipality Land Bureau measured the land, the defendant reported it in the name of her lover, Yinshan, in an attempt to seize the property. According to the law, since the defendant has remarried, her inheritance should be returned to provide for the plaintiff's livelihood. Therefore, she requests the court to order the defendant to return the two mu, four fen, three li, and one hao of land, half of the houses, and the contract to the plaintiff for management. The defendant, Jin Jinjie, also hired lawyer Zhou Yu to file a defense. Judge Han held a hearing yesterday afternoon, and both parties attended with their lawyers. The plaintiff Hou Liu stated the previous events and requested a judgment to return the land. The defendant, Jin Jinjie, testified that she was 48 years old and had not abused her mother. The judge said, "If you don't abuse the plaintiff on weekdays, why would she sue you?" She answered, "I support my mother." She also claimed that Jin Asan had been living in her house for 13 years. At this point, the defendant's lawyer stated that the plaintiff was a good person and the whole matter was stirred up by Hou Xiaomao. The judge ordered both parties to reconcile outside of court.

Exclusively Performing Exorcisms for Others

Banning Is Necessary

Wu Falin, a 47-year-old from Tongzhou, has no legitimate occupation and claims to be able to exorcise ghosts and cure diseases to collect money. Ignorant and foolish people believe this to be true. Recently, Wu has been performing his tricks extensively in the Qichangzhan area of Pudong. The sick are all deceived. It is necessary to ban this behavior. The seized items were confiscated. Wu and others obeyed meekly.

back was severely injured, and the case was bizarre and Bian's

ferocity was unheard of and extremely illegal. The police were dispatched to the address to arrest him, but Bian knew that the plan had failed and fled, so he was not caught.

Motorcycles

Second Race Encountered Heavy Rain 156

Belgian Minister Attended with Family

Third Race to Be Held Tomorrow Night

The Shanghai motorcycle race was held at Shen Garden yesterday (the 5th) evening for the second performance. Just as the race was about to begin, a sudden downpour lasted for half an hour before stopping, causing the track

to absorb water and become a muddy swamp. Cars driving on it sprayed mud, not only making it difficult for the racers but also dampening the spirits of the enthusiastic

Chinese and foreign spectators. However, the number of attendees was still very high, and the American consul and the Belgian minister attended with their families, showing that the amazing skills of these eleven daredevils had captured the hearts of the people, who were eager to see them. However, the riders were still brave and continued without fear. Although the program was not completed, their spirit of daring was admirable. Finally, to welcome the Belgian Minister, Mr. Scully held a flying start race for one lap. Mr. Scully ran it with full speed and was praised by the Belgian Minister. The time was 27 and 2/5 seconds. It was difficult to achieve this time on a muddy track. The third performance will be held this Sunday (the 8th) at 9:00 PM, rain or shine. Various machines have been repaired, and any heavy rain will not cause damage.

The Development of the Far East Comical Photo Advertising Company 157

Since inventing comical photo advertising, the Far East Comical Photo Advertising Company has received many orders from both local and foreign clients, because it is very capable of attracting the attention of the audience. Bayer Pharmaceutical Factory's Aspirin is managed by Qianxin Foreign Company. Considering the great effect of comical photo advertising, the company has specially ordered a large number of various and extremely hilarious photos from the company, which is expected to be displayed in various shop windows in the future, and passers-by will laugh without stopping.

Lost Boy Waiting to Be Claimed 158

The Municipal Public Security Bureau reported yesterday that the Second District sent a lost boy, Zhou Shizi, who was found in the Rihui Port area. According to the report, he is seven years old and from Funing. His father's name is Zhou Erda. This time, he was delivering food to the silk factory for his sister-in-law and lost his way home. The boy is wearing a blue cloth cotton jacket, blue cloth pants, and is barefoot. The boy is temporarily sent to Xinpu Hall to be cared for while waiting to be claimed.

The Anhui Jindou Five Counties Association held an executive committee meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday at 1124 Weishan Lane, Pingliang Road, Yangshupu, at the association's office. It was resolved to first send someone to investigate the incident and handle it according to law. The meeting adjourned after the agenda was completed.

Weather Report 161

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the sky was cloudy. North of Ma'an Island, the wind was light from the north to the northwest. To the south, there was a north or northeast wind. There was intermittent fog along the coast.
